To play ''//SEVEN//'' you will work in small groups to tell a story or reveal a process in //seven shots or less//. We will discuss the completed exercises during class and vote on a winner for each category. This game provides opportunities for students to learn 1) how to employ a variety of shots (Wide, Medium, Close), 2) how to create narrative meaning through image juxtaposition, 3) how to begin and end a scene/story/process, 4) how to economize in visual storytelling through the concept of "Montage", and 5) how to work as a team. [[PREPARATIONS]] Although both story and process show a series of actions or events, and each has a beginning and end, they have important differences. Like a story, a process includes a sequence of actions or steps which is eventually completed. However, a process needn't include a character, which means that often a process lacks a (character driven) plot, conflict, or obstacles. Even so, the details of a process, if captured effectively, can be involving or even entertaining. [[TYPES OF PROCESS]] Although both story and process show a series of actions or events, and each has a beginning and end, they have important differences. Stories involve one or more characters who encounter obstacles, and often the unfolding actions pose a question, puzzle, or mystery that is answered in the conclusion. For this reason a good story usually offers a more meaningful experience for the viewer. [[KEEP IT SIMPLE]] Since you're limited to seven shots, you should choose a SIMPLE story idea with one or at most two characters. Also consider the locations available on campus for this exercise. [[SAMPLE STORY IDEA]] //Getting a snack from a vending machine is an example of a simple process.// It involves finding a coin, inserting the coin into the slot, deciding on a selection, pressing the selection button, and retrieving the purchased item from the delivery tray. See a few types of process below. ''DIY'' (how to do or make something) ''Lost and Found'' (seeking, searching, and finding) ''The Problem'' (how to fix or repair something, or overcome an obstacle) ''The Journey'' (how to travel/move/go from here to there) ''The Change'' (how something changes from one state to another) STOP AND CONSIDER: To which category would the above described "vending machine" process belong? More than one? It's not unusual for a process to be a combination of the listed categories. [[SAMPLE PROCESS]] PAUSE HERE to discuss story ideas with your group. Like a process, if the plot of your story is too complex or sophisticated, it may not be suitable for this game. ''Keep it simple.'' And again, be mindful of the locations available on campus. DO THIS NOW: 1. Decide on a story. 2. Spend a few minutes refining and clarifying the plot of your story. What exactly happens? What are the actions, from beginning to end? 3. Break these actions down into individual shots by making a SHOT LIST using the provided hard copy form. Remember: ''You will edit in camera, so you must shoot in story order. '' [[A FEW RULES]] Here is an example of a simple story: //A young man dozes beneath a blanket, his head on a soft pillow. He abuptly awakens, switches off an alarm clock, then tosses off the covers to reveal he is fully clothed in a business suit. He rises to his feet, quickly arranging his necktie and hair while he grabs a briefcase and presses a "Lobby" button. An elevator door opens and he exits.// [[A FEW CONSIDERATIONS]] STOP HERE to discuss with your group the kinds of simple processes that can be shown within the limit of seven shots. CONSIDER: • To show or reveal a process you must carefully consider the sequence of actions or events from beginning to end. Is the process simple enough it can be revealed within the seven shot limit? Think carefully about the individual steps involved. • How is each step to be //visualized// through the lens of the camera? Wide Shot, Medium Shot, Closeup? Static or moving? Camera angle? DO THIS NOW: • Decide on a process. Keep in mind the locations available on campus for this exercise. • Consider the shot for each step, and using the provided form make a complete SHOT LIST. [[RULES]] Rules to keep in mind: 1. Edit IN CAMERA when shooting. //You must shoot in process order.// 2. No sound is to be recorded or used. 3. Employ a variety of shots (wide, medium, close). 4. Finished running length of all shots together should be 60 seconds or less. 5. Each group has 2.5 hours (150 minutes) to complete the game once started. [[BEGIN THE GAME]] A few rules to keep in mind: 1. One or two characters. 2. Edit IN CAMERA when shooting. //You must shoot in story order.// 3. No sound is to be recorded or used. //This means no dialogue.// 4. Employ a variety of shots (wide, medium, close). 5. Finished running length of all shots together should be 60 seconds or less. 6. Each group has 2.5 hours (150 minutes) to complete the game once started. [[START THE GAME]] 1. Transport your gear to the campus location needed. 2. One member of your group should have a smartphone so you can continue to access the game during shooting. 3. Setup and securely stage your equipment. 4. Assign crew roles: Director, Camera Operator, Camera Asst, Talent //Rotate crew roles for each shot, so every group member has the opportunity to experience the job duties of every role at least alt="Coffee Process" /> </div> </body> </html> [[A FEW COMMENTS]] This series of images shows that coffee beans are harvested, roasted, ground, and brewed before the finished product is consumed. STOP AND CONSIDER: • No individual step of the process is explained or detailed. For instance, we don't see exactly how beans are roasted. That could be a process in and of itself. Instead, the process shown is a basic visual summary of the major steps from harvesting to consuming coffee. • Are seven images necessary to show the process? Could the series begin with the second image of a man picking beans? Could the series be reduced to only four images? If so, which four? DO THIS NOW: Take a moment with your group to make a reduced list of shots (in order). Use the SHOT BREAKDOWN form provided. • You will find that fewer shots may convey the //impression of a complete process//, even though each individual step isn't shown. This truth is at the heart of cinematic //Montage// and applies to every kind of visual storytelling. //Showing just a few select parts can offer the impression of the whole. // [[CHOOSE A PROCESS]] 1. Transport your gear to the campus location needed. 2. One member of your group should have a smartphone so you can continue to access the game during shooting. 3. Setup and securely stage your equipment. 4. Assign crew roles: Director, Camera Operator, Camera Asst, Talent //Rotate crew roles for each shot, so every group member has the opportunity to experience the job duties of every role at least once.// [[WHILE SHOOTING]] DURING SHOOTING: • Rehearse ''BEFORE'' you record each shot. • The total allotted time (150 minutes) divided by the number of shots (7) allows for (text-style:"underline")[around 20 minutes per shot]. So have one group member watch the time. • Use your ''SHOT LIST'' to make notes and check off completed shots. • ''ALWAYS'' playback recorded shots to check focus and exposure, before moving on to the next shot. [[WHEN YOU'RE FINISHED]] REMINDERS WHILE SHOOTING: • Rehearse ''BEFORE'' you record each shot. • The total allotted time (150 minutes) divided by the number of shots (7) allows for (text-style:"underline")[around 20 minutes per shot]. So have one group member watch the time. • Use your ''SHOT LIST'' to make notes and check off completed shots. • ''ALWAYS'' playback recorded shots to check focus and exposure, before moving on to the next shot. [[WHEN YOU'RE FINISHED]] • Each group will be alloted 30 minutes to prepare before starting the game. • Select a category below - PROCESS or STORY - and proceed. • Read the following passages carefully. All group members must be comfortable with the pace. (text-style:"underline")[//You can always return to this starting place using the back/return arrow button on each page.//] [[PROCESS]] [[STORY]] • Whether you classify this as a scene or story, it conveys a simple idea and provides a surprise within the unfolding circumstances. • The story is written to reveal specific information with each successive action. We don't even suspect we're in an elevator until the "Lobby" button is mentioned. By witholding information from the reader (viewer) until a certain point in the story, we create a moment of discovery. • Just as the writing reveals only partial information, action by action, individual shots can do the same. • The above described actions are easily broken down into individual shots. DO THIS NOW: Using the provided hard copy SHOT BREAKDOWN form, take a few minutes to assign shots to specific portions of the description. How many shots have you listed? [[CHOOSE YOUR STORY]] When you have completed your shots - and checked them with playback - please do the following: • Stow all equipment in bags and cases. Double-check inventory before leaving the shooting location. • Return to the Sound Stage with your gear and stow it neatly on one of the carts. • Remove your SD card from the DSLR camera, lock it, and give it to the instructor. [[GETTING STARTED]]
